The hardest part about being a woman of color is having to take ownership for being different. You can be confident, accomplished, successful and be the person who has worked to deserve the opportunity, but because your image doesn't fit the "desired" narrative, you can easily be denied the opportunity or discriminated against. On one hand you want to be optimistic and extremely positive that your day and proper recognition will come; but on the other hand, a part of you may have to prepare for disappointments and rejections because historically the stats demonstrate that being different doesn't always translate with having access to certain opportunities or reaching a particular salary threshold.

While I understand Taraji's hurt, she really needs to realize that some movies simply do not sell/translate overseas. Does she watch foreign productions? Some foreign films can be sold in the US while others simply cannot.  Will "Color Purple" have a large audience in China? No, it does not translate there. Will "Color Purple" have a large audience in the Middle East? No, it does not translate there. In Australia and NZ? No, it does not translate there. In Europe? No, it does not translate there. Latin America? Also no. In Nigeria? Not even there. Why? Because the Nigerian local industry produces more films than Bollywood.   Now, can the studios sell movies, such as "Dune", to Asian, the Middle Eastern, European, and other markets? Most definitely! Movies like that DO translate overseas. If Taraji were in that movie, she WILL BE making a lot of money (assuming her team really fights for her).  Movies = products Products = sales  The more sellable/translatable movie is, the more money it generates everywhere (both domestic and foreign markets).  Finally, she lives in California, a state with incredibly high taxation.   It's simple Finance 101. What does she not understand?

I can't speak on actors but across the board in the industry, we're all getting killed with our rates, union or not... while executive pay is going up exponentially, literally taking it from all of us.  My union (IATSE) LOSES money every negotiation... I was part of layoffs because my salary rolled over plus 3% cost of living increase; amazing review, promotion a month later... then two months later, laid-off in a salary dump.  Now, the "minimum" rate per day is $100 less than when it was when I started 20 years ago.  Not the same or more... $100 less.     She won't quit, and I won't quit... because we all LOVE what we do, it's in us to create... and executives at studios and production companies use that against us, knowing there's a line of people around the block begging for these jobs.  But, she's 100% right in that it's hard to make a living here in LA and afford a mortgage here for some 'just decent' neighborhood.  People outside of our industry and city think it's so "rich" and glamorous to work in this industry but it's really not... it's fun but it's hard to make ends meet here at almost any payrate.

OK -- so who EXACTLY is she getting paid less than? Give me examples. Look: It's called business. And as much as she thinks she's a star, she isn't. She's a great actress. But if you put her in a lineup of 100 actresses, few would be able to point her out, even fewer would know her name. That goes for thousands  and thousands of actors and actresses. Until she's the star -- Empire wasn't her show; Hidden Figures was not her movie -- and she rakes in huge numbers when her movies open, she will get paid what her agents get her. And that latter part cannot be emphasized enough. You don't like what you get? Fire your agent. Unless you have them onboard out of sympathy or pity, your agents are mostly to blame for the money you're making. I mean, you do realize she's a union member, right? She's getting paid her legally contracted dues. And true story: oscars and emmys mean nothing more than pats on the back and a possible -- read low -- pay increase. But if you go back 20, 30 years, look at actors who won awards, you're going to come away going, "Oh yea -- I forgot about them." My background is box office analytics. Taraji has minimal clout. And her ego needs to understand that. Her ego needs to know she's talented, but talent is second fiddle to if your movie was a 10 multiplier. Her ego needs to know that her whining about working hard? George Clooney just had to give up his director's fee to get a movie made. Mega star Clooney had to hustle. Spielberg got turned down left-and-right for Lincoln. Hustle. The star system has been dead for 20 years and Taraji was never one to begin with. So yea -- she's gotta work her butt off. So again: check the ego, fire your agent, and start making things that make a crap ton of money. Or just live within your means understanding you'll always get hired, and you'll make what you're worth and entitled to in show BUSINESS.

Shalom unto you all and many blessings to you and to your beautiful families.   This beautiful woman of substance has the right to feel what she is feeling.  And the man of valour also spoke truth. I do not disagree with what has been shared in this intimate dialogue.  The biased treatment that takes place within this particular realm of influence against people of black descent has everything to do with truth about our original history as a nation of people.   Many in the world of entertainment know who we are, especially those who are set up in positions with "leverage and dominance" (those who are able to control the narrative when it comes to how people of black descent are seen within this realm of influence).  This is why I speak the way I do when it comes to the world of entertainment. I do not speak to degrade or demean those who are a part of this particular world.  But I do speak against how people are treated in their value in this industry, especially when it comes to their distinction in image and when it comes to the value of their gifts, skills, talents, and abilities.  The entertainment industry was never designed to take on the image it has embraced. But it has been mishandled by so many people who sat and still sit in certain positions of authority. And people of black descent have been "secretly" targeted in this world for a very long time. It has been hard to detect by many who are on the outside looking in. Because it has been hidden well behind the "glam, the glitter, the excitement, and the images of what dreams and fame has been sold off to look like.   Only if people knew the actual experiences many of our people go through in this industry in order to make it. Some are manipulated and persuaded to do some very demeaning and inhumane things to be significant and famous. And it is done that way on purpose so the truth about their value in image can be mocked, reviled, and disrespected, along with the enrichment of their original history as a nation of people. These particular "circle of people" in authority feel like as long as they throw a few dollars in the direction of our people who are a part of this industry, they can continue with the degradation and with the misgovernment of our value as a people.   Money is not the issue in this industry. The issue lies in how the value of a human soul is seen, especially the value of a soul that is of black descent.  Anytime a dollar is put up against the actual value of a human soul, especially one that is of black descent, it reveals a very telling truth about the souls affected by these manipulative agendas. It exposes the presence of a real truth about our worth as a nation of people. And a "dollar" is used to control the narrative of that truth.  When in fact the original weight of our influence is not found in a "dollar." And they know it. What we carry outweighs the value of a dollar. What we carry is weighty enough to change the world without currency. And that is a very deep truth. Money is used in this world to keep people under an unhealthy control. Money is not the menace or the villain in this story. Ignorance is the menace in this story. Because if ignorance can make a certain group of people show disregard to the actual value of a human soul, especially the souls of those of black descent, then it exposes how they see their own value in this area.  God Bless you all and Shalom unto you and to your beautiful families.
